NOTICE OF MOTION

TAKE NOTICE that application will be made to the above Honourable Court as
a matter of urgency at 10h00 on 16 April 2026, or as soon thereafter as counsel
may be heard, for an order in the following terms:
1

Dispensing the time periods, forms and manner of service provided for in
the Uniform Rules of the Court and condoning non-compliance with the
rules due to urgency in terms of Rule 6(12);

2

Issuing a rule nisi calling upon the respondent to appear and show cause,
at a date and time to be determined by this Honourable Court, why a final
order should not be made in the following terms:

2.1

Interdicting and restraining the respondent from disclosing,
disseminating, publishing, or communicating to any third party,
including but not limited to the Public Servants Association of South
Africa (PSA), the National Education Health and Allied Workers
Union (NEHAWU), the Democratic Nursing Organisation of South
Africa (DENOSA), the Police and Prisons Civil Rights Union

AFR1282 Notice of Motion Final 16.04.2026(3791512.1)

001-2

001-3
16/4/2026-2:55:28 PM

(POPCRU), the Federation of Unions of South Africa (FEDUSA), or
any other trade union, any confidential, proprietary, or commercially
sensitive information belonging to the applicant or any of its
subsidiaries, including any document referred to as the “Mahlangu
Root Cause Analysis” or “Mahlangu RCA”, or any information
relating to the applicant’s internal systems, clinical processes,
financial affairs, or integration architecture;
2.2

Interdicting and restraining the respondent from making, publishing,
or causing to be published any defamatory, false, or malicious
statements concerning the applicant, its directors, officers,
employees, auditors, or any regulatory bodies, including but not
limited to any statement referred to as a “Whistleblower’s Manifesto”
or any public statement alleging fraud, market deception,
misconduct, or impropriety on the part of the applicant or any person
associated with it;

NOTICE OF INTENTION TO OPPOSE

TO: THE REGISTRAR OF THE ABOVE HONOURABLE COURT
AND TO: DENEYS INC, ATTORNEYS FOR THE APPLICANT
(Email: jason.whyte@deneys.co.za)

KINDLY TAKE NOTICE that:
1.
The Respondent, WILBUR WILLIAM MATTHEE, hereby gives notice of his intention to
oppose the urgent application brought by the Applicant in the above-captioned matter.
2.
The Respondent is a self-represented litigant. His address for service of all further process
and documents in this matter is:
15 Bellevue Street
Voorbrug

Page 15 of 159

007-1

007-2

16

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
Cape Town
7001
Email: info@ethichawks.co.za

3.
The Respondent will deliver a full Answering Affidavit in due course, in accordance with
such timetable as this Honourable Court may determine. The Respondent requests a reasonable
opportunity of not less than 48 to 72 hours within which to do so.
4.

The Respondent further intends to raise, inter alia, the following points in limine:
4.1 The matter was served on the Respondent at approximately 21:42 on 15 April 2026, less
than 16 hours before the scheduled hearing, rendering it impossible for the Respondent to
obtain legal representation or prepare a considered response. The urgency, to the extent it
exists, is entirely self-created by the Applicant who was aware of the Respondent's forensic
findings since at least October 2025. This constitutes an abuse of court process.
4.2 Service did not comply with the requirements of Rule 4 of the Uniform Rules of Court in
that the Respondent was not properly served in a manner affording him adequate opportunity
to oppose.
4.3 The Applicant has failed to make out a case for urgent relief in accordance with the
requirements of Rule 6(12), in particular by relying on urgency that is self-created.

5.

The Respondent places the Applicant and this Honourable Court on notice that:
5.1 The settlement demand of R7,307,642.72 is a quantified legal claim for occupational
detriment, unlawful salary deductions, and related statutory breaches, which claims are
formally before the Labour Court (Case Nos. 2026-077546 and 2026-083299). Seeking
settlement of a legitimate and pending legal claim does not constitute extortion under South
African law.
5.2 The Respondent's disclosures constitute Protected Disclosures within the meaning of the
Protected Disclosures Act 26 of 2000 ("PDA") and concern systemic clinical and financial
governance failures affecting 1.9 million GEMS beneficiaries.
5.3 The Respondent denies that any intended disclosure involves or requires the release of
individual patient medical records or "special personal information" as defined in section 26 of
the Protection of Personal Information Act 4 of 2013 ("POPIA"). The disclosure pertains to
systemic integration architecture failures between the Gexus and DMS platforms, actuarial
miscalculations, and governance failures — all matters of public interest.

WHEREFORE the Respondent respectfully requests this Honourable Court to:

Page 16 of 159

007-2

007-3

17

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
(a) Postpone the hearing of the urgent application for a period of not less than 48 to 72 hours
to enable the Respondent to obtain legal representation and to prepare and deliver a full
Answering Affidavit;
(b) In the alternative, strike the application from the urgent roll on the grounds of self-created
urgency and/or abuse of process; and
(c) Grant any further and/or alternative relief as this Honourable Court deems fit.

DATED AT CAPE TOWN ON THIS 16 DAY OF APRIL 2026

_________________________________
WILBUR WILLIAM MATTHEE

ANSWERING AFFIDAVIT

I, the undersigned,
WILBUR WILLIAM MATTHEE
do hereby make oath and state that:

INTRODUCTION
1.
I am an adult male South African citizen with identity number 8909035151087. I reside at
15 Bellevue Street, Voorbrug, Cape Town, 7001. I am the Respondent in these proceedings. I
appear herein in person without legal representation, having been afforded insufficient time to
retain counsel following service of the application papers on me at approximately 21:42 on 15
April 2026.
2.
Save where the context indicates otherwise, the facts contained herein fall within my own
personal knowledge and are true and correct. Where I make submissions of a legal nature, I do so
on my own understanding and, to the extent necessary, reserve the right to supplement this affidavit
once I have obtained legal representation.

Page 18 of 159

009-1

009-2

19

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM

3.
I confirm that I hold a Postgraduate Diploma in Health Services Management (NQF Level
8, CPUT), a BTech in Psychiatric Nursing/Midwifery/Community Nursing and Communication,
and am a Specialist Registered Nurse with approximately 18 years of clinical governance
experience. I am the founder of EthicHawks Forensic Governance and Compliance Consultancy.
4.
This affidavit is deposed in opposition to the Applicant's urgent application for an interim
interdict (rule nisi). I oppose both the procedural basis of the application (urgency and service) and
its substantive merits.

POINT IN LIMINE: URGENCY AND SERVICE
5.
I raise the following points in limine which are dispositive of the application at the
threshold:
5.1.
THE PUBLIC RECORD: The information the Applicant seeks to interdict is already
contained in my served and filed Statement of Claim in the Labour Court and my Section 162
Application in the High Court. Under the principle of open justice, these are public documents.
One cannot interdict the disclosure of information that is already sitting in the public court files.
This application is a redundant attempt to 'un-ring a bell' that has already been rung.
5.2.
SELF-CREATED URGENCY: The Applicant was aware of my forensic findings
regarding the Gexus/DMS integration failure, the alleged governance failures at GEMS, and my
protected disclosure concerns since at least October/November 2025. The Applicant's attorneys,
Deneys, sent a cease-and-desist letter on 15 April 2026 at what appears to be business hours,
indicating awareness of the matter throughout the day. The application papers were only served
on me at approximately 08:53 on 16 April 2026. The Applicant has accordingly manufactured its
own urgency by delaying service to prevent me from obtaining legal representation. This
constitutes an abuse of the rules of court. I refer this Court to the authority in Salt and Another v
Smith 1991 (2) SA 186 (NmHC) and the principle established in Luna Meubels Vervaardigers
(Edms) Bpk v Makin and Another 1977 (4) SA 135 (W), that urgency must not be self-created.
5.3
IMPROPER SERVICE: The papers were served on me less than 2 hours before the
scheduled hearing on 16 April 2026. Under Rule 6(12)(b) of the Uniform Rules of Court, an
applicant in urgent proceedings is required to set out explicitly the reasons why service in the
ordinary manner is not appropriate and to ensure that the respondent has a reasonable opportunity
to prepare. No adequate opportunity was afforded to me to prepare or to brief counsel. The service
is accordingly defective and the application falls to be struck from the roll. The Applicant’s conduct
in serving the finalized papers at 08:53 AM for a 10:00 AM hearing is a gross violation of the
Uniform Rules of Court. It is physically and legally impossible for a respondent to read, digest,
and reply to a complex High Court application in 67 minutes. This is a deliberate attempt to
'steamroll' a self-represented whistleblower and obtain an order by default."

SUBSTANTIVE RESPONSE TO FOUNDING AFFIDAVIT
A. The Settlement Demand is a Quantified Legal Claim, Not Extortion

Page 19 of 159

009-2

009-3

20

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
6.
The Applicant's characterisation of my settlement demand of R7,307,642.72 as "extortion"
(para 9, 49, 51 of the founding affidavit) is denied and is legally incorrect. The demand is a fully
itemised and legally quantified claim for:
6.1 Direct Restitution (R1,027,107.12): Comprising 24 months of back-pay/substitution arising
from the unlawful salary deductions and constructive dismissal.
6.2 Property Loss (R145,000.00): Representing the total loss of fixed property directly
resulting from the Applicant's occupational detriment.
6.3 Professional Death Compensation (R5,135,535.60): A 10-year compensatory future loss of
earnings claim arising from the permanent destruction of my professional career and reputation
by the Applicant's conduct.
6.4 Clinical Provision (R750,000.00): A 10-year specialist psychosocial and clinical care fund
to address the profound PTSD and psychiatric injury resulting from targeted occupational
detriment.
6.5 Statutory Costs (R250,000.00): Representing the forensic audit costs and operational
expenses of EthicHawks incurred in documenting the systemic failures and governance
breaches.
7.
These claims are substantially identical to the claims formally filed in the Labour Court
under Case Nos. 2026-077546 (BCEA section 77A claim for unlawful salary deductions) and
2026-083299 (Statement of Claim for constructive dismissal and related claims, filed 9 April
2026). The Applicant's own founding affidavit acknowledges these proceedings at paragraph 25.

8.
The R7.3 million referenced by the Applicant is not a 'demand for silence' (extortion). It is
the prayed-for relief in my pre-existing Labour Court litigation for lost income and benefits due to
the Applicant's occupational detriment against me. Seeking the resolution of a pending legal claim
is a standard litigation procedure, not a criminal act.

9.
It is a fundamental principle of our law that an offer to settle a legitimate legal claim which
is already before a court, even in robust or forceful terms, does not constitute extortion. The
demand was not for money to suppress a fabricated claim — it was a settlement proposal backed
by pending litigation. Seeking to resolve legitimate legal claims through settlement is not only
lawful, but is encouraged by our courts. I refer to Nortje en 'n Ander v Prokureur-Generaal, Kaap
1978 (2) SA 659 (C) on the distinction between threats of harm and assertions of legal rights.
10.
The Applicant conflates the forcefulness of my communications, born of genuine distress
and occupational injury, with criminal conduct. The language I used in my emails of 14 and 15
April 2026 was urgent and direct. It was not a threat to cause unlawful harm — it was a declaration
that I would exercise lawful statutory and regulatory rights. This distinction is legally critical.

B. The Forensic Disclosure Does Not Threaten Individual Patient Data
11.
The Applicant's suggestion (paras 46, 47, 73.1 of the founding affidavit) that my proposed
disclosure constitutes a threatened breach of POPIA in respect of 1.9 million GEMS beneficiaries

Page 20 of 159

009-3

009-4

21

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
is denied, is misleading to this Court, and is designed to manufacture a basis for irreparable harm
that does not in fact exist.
12.
The "Mahlangu RCA" and "forensic payload" to which the Applicant refers are documents
relating to a systemic clinical integration failure between the Gexus and DMS software platforms
operated by Medscheme. The documents:
12.1
Demonstrate that an automated "non-adherence letter" was erroneously generated
and sent to a GEMS member (Mrs Mahlangu) due to an integration gap between Gexus and
DMS — not any action by the member.
12.2
Identify a structural governance failure in how the two platforms communicate
patient medication benefit category changes.
12.3
Constitute an internal root cause analysis reflecting systemic operational risk — not
a document containing the individual health records of 1.9 million beneficiaries.
13.
The disclosure I intend to make to trade unions and regulators concerns: (a) the existence
of a systemic integration gap; (b) its financial and clinical implications; and (c) the fact that the
Board appears to have been aware of this risk and failed to disclose it as a material governance
matter. This is a matter of institutional and governance-level information, not a data dump of
patient records.
14.
Accordingly, the POPIA argument raised by the Applicant is a deliberate overstatement
intended to frighten this Court into granting relief. I deny that any POPIA breach is intended or
would result from the disclosures I propose to make.

C. The Terminological Correction Evidences Good Faith
15.
The Applicant relies heavily (paras 36, 37, 58 of the founding affidavit) on my email of 15
April 2026 (Annexure GVW5) in which I corrected my use of the word "leakage."
16.
This correction is evidence of my forensic credibility and good faith, not — as the Applicant
suggests — of a concession that undermines my case. The correction was a voluntary
terminological refinement made in the interests of precision:
16.1
The word "leakage" implied money physically leaving the scheme through fraud or
misappropriation.
16.2
What I documented is more accurately described as: (a) erosion of member day-today benefits; (b) corruption of claims data; (c) operational waste; and (d) plausible inflation of
total claims expenditure — arising from the systemic Gexus/DMS integration gap.
16.3
The financial impact — an inflated claims environment contributing to the 9.5%
premium increase borne by 1.9 million government employees — remains documented and
unchanged.

Page 21 of 159

009-4

009-5

22

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
17.
A whistleblower who voluntarily corrects imprecise language before any court intervention
is demonstrating exactly the kind of good faith that the PDA and our courts seek to encourage. The
Applicant's attempt to weaponized this correction as an admission of bad faith or absence of
evidence is rejected.

D. The Protected Disclosures Act Defence
18.
The Applicant argues at paragraph 52 of the founding affidavit that neither the Companies
Act 71 of 2008 nor the Protected Disclosures Act 26 of 2000 affords protection to disclosures made
by a person who, at the time of the disclosure, is no longer an employee.
19.

This legal submission is disputed. I submit as follows:
19.1
The PDA defines "employee" in section 1 as including a "former employee."
Section 1 read with section 3 of the PDA extends protection to disclosures made by former
employees in respect of improper conduct that occurred during their employment.
19.2
The information I possess and propose to disclose was obtained during my
employment with Medscheme in my capacity as Care Coordinator/Case Manager dealing with
GEMS member clinical claims. The improper conduct (the Gexus/DMS integration failure and
the governance failures surrounding it) occurred during and continued beyond my employment.
19.3
The fact that my employment has ended does not extinguish my statutory duty to
report improper conduct that affects public health and safety. The Mahlangu case involves the
clinical management of a GEMS beneficiary. Failure to disclose a known systemic risk to
patient clinical outcomes is a patient safety issue which I, as a registered healthcare
professional, am obligated to report under the Nursing Act 33 of 2005 and the Health
Professions Act 56 of 1974.

20.
Even if the PDA protection were found not to apply (which is denied), the common law
right of a citizen to approach regulatory and oversight bodies, trade unions, and public institutions
with evidence of governance failures is well established. The Applicant is not entitled to a court
order preventing a citizen from exercising these rights.

E. The Public Interest Dimension
21.
The Applicant characterises my disclosures as purely self-interested and designed to coerce
payment. This is denied. The following public interest considerations are relevant to this Court's
exercise of its discretion:
21.1
GEMS is a medical scheme serving approximately 1.9 million government
employees, including nurses, police officers, teachers, and other essential workers. The clinical
integrity of GEMS's administration is a public interest matter of the highest order.
22.2
The 9.5% premium increase approved for 2026 (as referenced in Actuarial Practice
Note 303 — "APN 303") requires justification on the basis of accurate claims data. If the
Gexus/DMS integration gap has contributed to inflated claims data that underpinned this
increase, GEMS members are entitled to know this.

2. In the alternative, postpone the matter for a period of not less than 48 to 72 hours to enable

policy-blind.

SUPPLEMENTARY ANSWERING AFFIDAVIT
I, the undersigned, WILBUR WILLIAM MATTHEE, do hereby make oath and state:

1. INTRODUCTION, PROFESSIONAL STANDING, AND DESTITUTION
1.1 I am an adult male Specialist Registered Nurse (NQF Level 8) and hold a
Postgraduate Diploma in Health Services Management. I am also a Forensic
Governance Specialist and the founder of EthicHawks Forensic Governance and
Compliance Consultancy.
1.2 I appear in person because I am destitute. I have no income, no transport money, and
cannot afford legal representation. I attach a separate Affidavit of Destitution
marked "WW6".
1.3 This affidavit supplements my answering affidavit filed on 16 April 2026. I reserve the
right to supplement further upon obtaining legal representation and discovery.

2. THE APPLICANT'S BAD FAITH: CONTRASTING DR OHM'S LETTER WITH
THE OPPOSING AFFIDAVIT
2.1 I attach as Annexure RESU1 a letter of recommendation from Dr P.M.J. Ohm, a team
leader medical doctor practising at Mitchells Plain District Hospital Emergency
Unit, where I work as a shift leader. Dr Ohm states that I have "depth of clinical
knowledge", "de-escalate any heated situation with a calm tone and demeanour",

Supplementary Answering Affidavit – Respondent in Person

Page 33 of 159

Page 3 of 17

012-1

012-2

34

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
Matthee v AfroCentric Investment Corporation Limited | Case No. 2026-086906 | Western Cape High
Court
and "protect patient dignity". This letter constitutes objective, professional evidence
of my competence, good faith, and mental fitness.
2.2 In stark contrast, the Applicant — through its representative Mr Xolile Vincent
Manyati (a Senior Employee Relations Specialist who has never met me and is not a
medical professional) — deposed to an opposing affidavit in the CCMA matter
(Case No. WECT23564-25), one filed after my first Board-level escalation (see
Annexure GRC1 and GRC2). In that sworn affidavit, Mr Manyati stated under oath
that my documented PTSD and depression were "an excuse" and "an
afterthought" (see Annexure OA1, paragraph 6.3).
2.3 The Applicant has never produced any medical evidence contradicting my psychiatric
condition. A specialist psychiatrist's report confirming my diagnosis and
occupational detriment was provided to the Applicant. They have chosen to ignore
it.
2.4 This conduct constitutes bad faith — it is a reckless disregard for the truth, made under
oath. It demonstrates that the Applicant is prepared to swear to falsehoods to defeat a
whistleblower. This Honourable Court should take judicial notice of this pattern of
dishonesty when evaluating the Applicant's claim to "irreparable harm".

KEY LEGAL POINT — CLEAN HANDS DOCTRINE
A party seeking equitable relief must come to Court with clean hands. The Applicant's
willingness to contradict an uncontested psychiatric report under oath, through a
layperson deponent, denudes its application of the good faith necessary to sustain urgent
interdict relief. See: Setlogelo v Setlogelo 1914 AD 221 (requirements for interdict
include absence of undue hardship and clean hands).

3. POINTS IN LIMINE
3.1 Improper Service: The Applicant served its founding papers on me at 08:53 on 16
April 2026 for a hearing at 10:00 the same day — a period of only 67 minutes to
respond. I filed a notice to oppose and an answering affidavit, but could not attend
court because I am destitute. The Applicant's conduct constitutes an abuse of
process. The rule nisi should be discharged on this ground alone.
3.2 Self-Created Urgency: The Applicant was aware of my forensic findings since
October 2025. It chose to take no action until I set a deadline of 16 April 2026. The
urgency is entirely self-created and cannot found urgent relief. See: Luna Meubels

Vervaardigers (Edms) Bpk v Makin (t/a Makin's Furniture Manufacturers) 1977 (4)
SA 135 (W).

POINTS IN LIMINE — SUMMARY
This Honourable Court is respectfully invited to discharge the rule nisi on the following
preliminary grounds, without reaching the merits: (1) improper service — 67-minute
notice for an urgent hearing; (2) self-created urgency — applicant dormant since October
2025.

3A. FAILURE TO SATISFY INTERDICT REQUIREMENTS: EXISTENCE OF
ALTERNATIVE REMEDIES
3A.1 I respectfully submit that the Applicant's request for an interdict must fail as it cannot
prove the absence of an alternative satisfactory remedy. The Applicant is a
corporate employer with full access to standard internal disciplinary mechanisms
and the ordinary procedures of the Labour Court. By choosing to bypass its own
internal grievance and disciplinary frameworks — and instead dragging a destitute
former employee into the Urgent High Court on 67 minutes' notice — the
Applicant is attempting to weaponise this Court to suppress a statutory protected
disclosure. An urgent High Court interdict is not a substitute for standard dispute
resolution.

ALTERNATIVE REMEDY — LEGAL STANDARD
A fundamental requirement for final (and interim) interdict relief is that the applicant
must demonstrate the absence of an alternative, adequate remedy. See: Setlogelo v
Setlogelo 1914 AD 221; Olympic Passenger Services (Pty) Ltd v Ramlagan 1957 (2) SA
382 (D). The Applicant has access to its internal grievance mechanisms, the CCMA, and
the Labour Court — all of which are adequate alternative remedies. The Applicant's
deliberate election to bypass these constitutes an abuse of the urgent court roll.

4. QUANTIFICATION IN RESPONSE TO "UNQUANTIFIED" COMPLAINT
4.1 On 15 April 2026, Deneys Attorneys sent a letter (Annexure WW1) stating that my
demand was "unquantified" and that this supported an allegation of extortion.
4.2 In direct response, I sent a fully itemised quantification of R7,307,642.72 (Annexure
GVW4 to the founding affidavit).

4.3 That quantification was not a new demand. It was the first full Rand expression of the
same claim already filed in the Labour Court on 9 April 2026. My Labour Court
Statement of Claim expressly reserved the right to quantify (Annexure WW2).
4.4 A person engaged in extortion does not quantify at the request of the opposing
party. My conduct is that of a genuine litigant.

5. VOLUNTARY CORRECTION OF "LEAKAGE" — EVIDENCE OF GOOD
FAITH
5.1 The Applicant criticises me for using the word "leakage" and then correcting myself
(founding affidavit paras 36, 37, 58).
5.2 On 15 April 2026 at 20h44, I voluntarily sent a correction email (Annexure GVW5): "I
withdraw the word 'leakage' and regret any confusion caused. I do not withdraw my
complaint."
5.3 A bad-faith actor does not issue voluntary corrections. My correction is direct
evidence of good faith.

6. TRANSPARENCY: VOLUNTARY DISCLOSURE OF PENDING TRIAL
6.1 In January 2024, during recruitment, I voluntarily disclosed a pending trial relating to
blood alcohol levels to the Applicant's Human Capital department (Annexure
WW3). I provided an updated CV before employment.
6.2 The Applicant initially recruited me for the post of Specialist Care Manager.
6.3 However, at the point of signing the employment agreement, the Applicant unexpectedly
presented me with a contract reflecting the diminished title of "Care
Coordinator", without any prior consultation or explanation for this sudden
alteration.
6.4 Subsequently, during a recorded meeting ‘naming convention’ with the Operational
Manager and Human Capital, this discrepancy was formally addressed and my title
was rightfully updated to reflect my NQF Level 8 qualification, establishing my
correct designation as Case Manager.
6.5 The voluntary disclosure detailed in paragraph 6.1 is a demonstration of my radical
transparency. I bring this to the Court's attention to categorically state that the
pending trial is entirely irrelevant to these proceedings, involves no element of
dishonesty or extortion, and cannot be used by the Applicant to retroactively
impugn my character or my actions as a whistleblower.

7. PROCEDURAL INTEGRITY: RETRACTION OF MY OWN GRC ESCALATION
7.1 On 16 December 2025, I sent a GRC Escalation to the Board. When I realised it was
sent on a public holiday — invalidating my deadline — I immediately retracted it
and apologised (Annexure WW4).
7.2 A vexatious litigant does not retract his own documents. I respect process and have
demonstrated this consistently.

8. NECESSITY AND PROPORTIONALITY OF MY TONE
8.1 Between October 2025 and April 2026, I exhausted all internal remedies: grievances,
Board escalation, a letter to the Group CEO. The Applicant responded with silence,
suppression, and a CEO who breached my confidentiality.
8.2 By April 2026, the 9.5% premium increase had been approved. The Department of
Employment and Labour refused to unblock my benefits (Annexure WW5).
8.3 My explicit tone was necessary and proportionate. I threatened no violence or
unlawful act — only protected disclosures to trade unions and regulators, which are
expressly contemplated by the Protected Disclosures Act 26 of 2000.

9. PUBLIC INTEREST: APN 303 AND THE R3 BILLION "GOVERNANCE TAX"
9.1 At paragraph 40 of their Founding Affidavit, the Applicant admits that the Gexus and
DMS platforms manage chronic care pathways and adherence data. Actuaries rely
entirely on Gexus/DMS data to build statutory financial models under Actuarial
Practice Note 303 (APN 303).
9.2 As proven in my Root Cause Analysis (Annexure VICT1), the systemic integration gap
generates false non-adherence data. Actuaries are compelled to apply maximum
APN 303 risk loading, inflating the premium increase from the CMS-stipulated
3.3%–4% to 9.8% then refuced to 9.5%.%.

PUBLIC INTEREST — FISCAL QUANTUM
The excessive 4.5% premium inflation constitutes an artificial "Governance Tax"
costing approximately 1.9 million GEMS members an estimated R3.016 billion
annually. This is a matter of overwhelming public interest directly relevant to the
Applicant's claim that it suffers any harm from my disclosures.

10. NO POPIA BREACH
10.1 I intend to disclose systemic governance failures, not individual patient records. The
POPIA argument advanced by the Applicant is a deliberate overstatement designed
to suppress legitimate whistleblowing activity.

11. THE PROTECTED DISCLOSURES BILL, 2026 — PUBLIC POLICY AND
PROPORTIONALITY
11.1 On 8 April 2026, the Minister of Justice and Constitutional Development published the
Protected Disclosures Bill, 2026 for public comment. The Bill proposes to repeal
the existing PDA and introduce, inter alia, financial awards for whistleblowers of up
to 25% of any monetary sanction imposed on an employer as a result of a
protected disclosure.
11.2 The Bill was driven by the Zondo Commission's findings that the current Act does not
sufficiently protect whistleblowers. The Minister explicitly stated that the Bill aims
to "incentivise our whistleblowers" and that "the person who has made the
disclosure could receive an amount that does not exceed one fourth of the monetary
sanction".

POLICY PROPORTIONALITY ARGUMENT
If Parliament considers it legitimate to reward whistleblowers with up to 25% of
recovered funds (which on R3.016bn would equal R754 million), the Applicant's
characterisation of my R7,307,642.72 claim (representing less than 0.24% of the annual
waste exposed) as "extortion" is not only legally flawed — it is policy-blind and
contrary to the express direction of national legislation.

12. PUBLIC POLICY AND THE NATIONAL HEALTH INSURANCE (NHI) ACT
12.1 The National Health Insurance Act 20 of 2023 aims to achieve universal access to
quality healthcare. Its success depends entirely on the integrity of health data and
governance systems.
12.2 The systemic Gexus/DMS integration gap corrupts clinical data, leading to operational
waste and inflated claims. The R3.016 billion Governance Tax is a direct threat to
the NHI's fiscal sustainability.

PART Q: COUNTER-APPLICATION FOR DECLARATORY RELIEF
(UNCONDITIONAL)
17.1 I hereby institute a counter-application for declaratory relief. This counterapplication is not conditional upon the Applicant proceeding with its main
application. I seek these declaratory orders independently, and the counterapplication will proceed even if the Applicant withdraws its main application under
Case No. 2026/086906
17.2 I submit that this Honourable Court has jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief in terms
of section 19(1)(a)(iii) of the Superior Courts Act, 2013, which provides that a
Division has jurisdiction over "the granting of declaratory orders". Furthermore, to
the extent the Applicant may argue that aspects of this counter-application touch
upon Labour Court jurisdiction, I rely on the doctrine of causa continentia. The
Applicant deliberately elected to institute these urgent proceedings in the High
Court, placing the factual matrix of my disclosures directly before this forum. It is in
the interests of justice, and to avoid a multiplicity of actions, that this Court disposes
of the counter-application within the very forum the Applicant itself chose.
17.3 I further submit that the relief sought is not abstract or hypothetical. There is a
tangible and immediate advantage to be obtained:
17.3.1 The declaratory orders will immediately break the administrative deadlock with
the Department of Employment and Labour, allowing me access to unlawfully
withheld statutory social security benefits (UIF, retirement funds);
17.3.2 The declaratory orders will vindicate my reputation and establish my good faith,
which the Applicant has falsely attacked in its founding papers and in the CCMA
proceedings.

brought within the same papers.

Bhisho (Case No. 148/2020), where the respondents filed a counter-application
within their answering affidavit seeking declaratory relief. The fact that my counterapplication is not conditional on the main application proceeding is consistent with
the inherent jurisdiction of this Court to grant declaratory relief whenever it is just
and convenient to do so.

stake. Consequently, their formal joinder is not required in law for this Court to
grant the declaratory relief against the Applicant.

· Directly engages the mandate of the Social & Ethics Committee (monitoring the company's activities
regarding the EEA and ethical conduct) and the Risk Committee (overseeing material legal and
reputational risk).
My urgent plea for interim relief to prevent destitution stands. This affidavit only heightens the
immediacy of the required intervention.
I therefore reiterate my request for the Board's committees to:
1. Acknowledge receipt of this escalating evidence.
1. Intervene to ensure an independent, external investigation into the entire matter.
2. Mandate the provision of interim relief (paid leave, hardship payment) to prevent irreversible personal
harm.
3. Review the strategy being employed by the company's legal and HR representatives in this matter.
The choice is now stark: the Board can oversee a fair, external process to resolve a serious internal
failure, or it can allow the company's resources to be used to litigate against an employee it has
harmed, guaranteeing greater public exposure and liability.
I remain available for any direct communication from the Board or its designated independent
representative.
Please note: To prevent another procedural deadlock like the 30-day institutional silence I experienced

7. PRIMARY LEGAL ARGUMENT: THE HARM WAS CONTINUOUS, RESETTING THE
REFERRAL CLOCK
7.1. Legal Principle: Where unfair labour practices constitute a continuing wrong, the 90day period for referral resets for as long as the conduct persists. The last act in the
continuum sets the clock Gauteng Department of Health v Tsomakae (GAJB 5554-16)
[2017].
7.2. Application: The Respondent's misconduct was a continuous course of conduct that
only culminated with the institutional bad faith and refusal to engage transparently in early
December 2025. My referral is therefore within 90 days of the last confirming act of the
continuing wrong.

8. ALTERNATIVE ARGUMENT: COMPELLING GOOD CAUSE FOR CONDONATION
Should the Commissioner find the continuous harm principle not fully applicable, I
demonstrate compelling good cause.

8.1. Reason for Delay – Exhaustion of Remedies: Any delay was due to my good-faith
exhaustion of every internal and governance channel, a process systematically thwarted by
the Respondent. The CCMA referral was a last resort made promptly once this became
clear.

8.2. Prospects of Success are Overwhelming: I possess direct evidence for each allegation
(payslips, screenshots, emails, medical certificates). The Respondent's affidavit avoids
engaging with this substance.

8.3. Prejudice: The prejudice to me—destitution, health crisis—if denied a hearing is

9. THE RESPONDENT’S CLAIM OF “PREJUDICE” IS WITHOUT MERIT AND
DEMONSTRATES ITS BAD FAITH

9.1. The Respondent claims in its affidavit (paragraph 9.1) that it will suffer “severe
prejudice” should my application proceed because it would need to use ”resources that
are Joburg based to fly to Cape Town to deal with this unsubstantiated dispute.”

9.2. This claim is disingenuous and reveals the Respondent’s true disregard for the
seriousness of this matter and the imbalance of power:

a. **Relative Prejudice is Wholly Mismatched:** The Respondent, a large JSE-listed
corporate entity, complains of the administrative and financial inconvenience of
travel. I, an individual employee, am facing**actual destitution, inability to afford
food and medication, and severe health deterioration**. To equate corporate travel
logistics with the threat to an individual’s basic survival and health is not only
irrational but morally indefensible. Any prejudice to the Respondent is purely
financial and administrative; the prejudice to me is existential.

b. **The Respondent Created This Dispute Through Its Own Conduct:**The
Respondent’s suggestion that it is being held to ransom is an inversion of reality. The
dispute exists **solely because of the Respondent’s own actions**: its unlawful
deduction, its discriminatory conduct, its victimisation, and its systemic failure to
address my grievances. Having created the harm, it cannot now claim prejudice
when called to account for it.

c. **Travel is a Normal Business Cost in a National Company:** The Respondent, as a
national healthcare administrator, operates across the country. Requiring managers
to travel for a formal legal proceeding regarding serious misconduct within its ranks

Page 89 of 159

012-57

012-58

90

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM
is a normal cost of doing business and upholding the law. Framing this as an undue
burden is an admission that it views its own legal and ethical accountability as an
optional inconvenience.

D. **Modern Technology Provides Alternatives:** Should travel genuinely be a concern, the
Respondent could have explored or proposed virtual mediation or arbitration. Its failure to
do so and immediate leap to claiming “severe prejudice” underscores its strategy to use
cost as a barrier to justice.

d. **The Claim Undermines the CCMA’s Authority:** Implicit in the Respondent’s
argument is the suggestion that an employee in one city should be barred from
justice if the employer’s head office is in another. This strikes at the heart of the
CCMA’s national mandate to provide accessible dispute resolution for all
employees, regardless of geography.

9.3. Conclusion on Prejudice: The Respondent’s claim of prejudice is not a valid legal
objection but a tactical one, designed to portray me as an inconvenience rather than a
wronged employee seeking redress. The overwhelming and documented prejudice lies with
me. To deny condonation based on the Respondent’s purported travel costs would be a
grave miscarriage of justice, prioritising corporate convenience over an individual’s right to
be heard on matters of discrimination, victimisation, and survival.

10. CONCLUSION
10.1. My referral is, on the correct legal analysis, within time due to the continuous nature
of the harm. Alternatively, more than sufficient good cause exists.
10.2. To dismiss this application on a technicality would sanction the Respondent's
strategy of institutional bad faith and deny justice.

"administrative delay"—it is a Deemed Refusal to Act.
I require an immediate Statement of Position on the following three points of law:

Notice of Resignation (UI19) explicitly cited Automatically Unfair Constructive Dismissal due to a protected disclosure? By failing to intervene,
the DEL is allowing a false narrative to block my constitutional right to social security.
The Service Certificate Misrepresentation: The employer has issued a Certificate of Service (CERT1) that misrepresents the nature of my
departure and suppresses the occupational detriment I faced. I demand a Compliance Order to compel the correction of this statutory
document.
The UIF Non-Remittance (Criminality): My June 2025 records (and others) confirm deductions were made from my salary but never remitted
to the Fund. This is theft of statutory levies. Does the UIF department intend to prosecute this non-compliance, or is the whistleblower
expected to bear the cost of the employer's criminality?
I am a Specialist Registered Nurse (NQF 8) currently homelessness and a medically documented PTSD collapse (MED1) because I am being
denied access to my own security funds. Your department’s inaction is the primary driver of this human rights violation.
If I do not receive a Case Reference Number and a Compliance Order regarding the June 2025 UIF gap by Thursday, 16 April 2026, at 14:30, I
will:
Initiate an Urgent Mandamus Application in the High Court to compel the Department to perform its statutory duties.
Submit this entire chain of ignored correspondence to Daily Maverick and AmaBhungane as evidence of institutional failure.

The communication originated from DMS.

3. Root Cause Analysis

Miscommunication between Gexus and DMS systems.
Member collected cholesterol medication from acute benefit from 21/11/2017 until 17/12/2024.
From January 2025, medication was claimed under chronic benefit.
Although Gexus shows a chronic claim on 14/04/2023 onwards for cholesterol medication, DMS did not
receive this update.
DMS continued tracking adherence based on acute claims only, ignoring chronic claims after the benefit
change.
This resulted in the member being incorrectly flagged as non-adherent, despite being compliant.

The comms went out correctly, this member is non-adherent.

The non-adherent methodology is you need claim twice in a rolling three months member only claimed once in
the past 3 months.

Sep – No claims = 0
Aug – claims = 1
Jul – no claims =0
June – claims = 1
May – claims = 1

Please note a member could have claimed this month but the previous two months have not claims the
member will be flagged as non-adherent – and clinically and behaviourally there is a problem that requires
attention, therefore the intervention and should please be managed as such in the ADRM calls too.

I wanted to provide an update on the recent complaint investigation. Based on the information received, the
team indicated that the non-adherence correspondence was sent due to the member not claiming twice within
a three-month period, which aligns with the non-adherence methodology for the Jul–Sep 2025 period.

•

DMS began flagging the member as non-adherent in Dec 2024, after the last acute claim.

recognize this change.
•
As a result, automated non-adherence letters were sent on 19 May 2025 and 19 Oct 2025, despite the
member being compliant.

itself. Evidence supporting this timeline has beenPage

To whom it may concern,

It is my pleasure to write you a short motivation for Mr Wilbur William Matthee. My Name is Dr
Priscilla MiJeong Ohm currently working with Mr Matthee within the Mitchell’s Plain District hospital
Emergency unit. The emergency unit is one that requires timeous action, fast thinking and definitive
action as it has many moving parts including a high patient load, critically ill patients with
undifferentiated pathology all needing urgent management. Mr Matthee carries all the above
qualities. As a shift leader he allocates staff to needed areas with good skills distribution across the
floor, furthermore he often fills in gaps needed as they arise to allow for continued workflow and
patient care allowing for staff breaks without disruption of patient care. All shift related issues
including high risk patients who have absconded, drug ordering, equipment issues as well as family
communication as needed are always appropriately done or escalated with timeous feedback given
to the doctor team leader. When students are allocated whether nursing, EMS or medical are within
the unit during his work he allocates tasks to aid their learning and supervises each student within
their patient care.
When it comes to patient care within the emergency unit, Mr Matthee shows depth of clinical
knowledge which allows him to identify critically ill patients, as well as pre-empt needed
management which allows for improve the efficiency of patient care within the unit. He is well
versed in the management protocols commonly used within the unit and is able to remind doctors of
when the next blood gases or ECGs are needed as well as the next step in management on the
protocol. All emergency room doctors leave the resus patients once stabilised in Mr Matthee’s care
till next review time with no doubt that they will be correctly monitored, cared for and that they will
be timeously informed if there is a change in condition.
One particular point of excellence for Mr Matthee is the way he is able to de-escalate any heated
situation within the emergency unit whether it be with family, staff or patients with a calm tone and
demeanour. He approaches all his patients with the same respect and as much as possible protects
their dignity with simple actions as always closing curtains, giving patients privacy when needed and
answering patient queries as well as informing family members of needed standard procedures. His
method of communication and interaction with his patients has been a lesson and reminder to me
to give good, individualised care and communication that maintains patient dignity and autonomy.

Regards,
Dr PMJ Ohm

TO: The South African Human Rights Commission — Western Cape Provincial Office
REF:
DATE: 13 March 2026
RE: COMPREHENSIVE UPDATE — FORENSIC PAYROLL ANOMALY, CCMA
INSTITUTIONAL BIAS, MULTI-BODY FAILURE, LABOUR COURT ACCESS
OBSTRUCTION, AND CONFIRMED IMMINENT HOMELESSNESS
Further to SAHRC correspondence of 10 February 2026 and Applicant update of 5 March 2026 | Matthee v
AfroCentric Health (RF) (Pty) Ltd & Others

Dear Commissioner / Legal Officer,
I write to provide a comprehensive update to this file. My update of 5 March 2026 documented the
collapse of the DEL and CCMA processes and my filing of an urgent Labour Court application. Since that
date, the situation has deteriorated significantly across every dimension — legally, financially, physically,
and personally. I place each development on formal record with documentary precision. I ask the SAHRC
to read this update not as a list of grievances but as a connected forensic account of what happens when
every statutory and civil society safety net fails simultaneously around a formally disabled whistleblower.

1. FORENSIC FINDING: STATUTORY PAYROLL MISREPRESENTATION — JULY 2025
Cross-referencing my July 2025 payslip against the Respondents' official UIF/SARS declarations has
revealed a material discrepancy that transforms the characterisation of the unlawful deduction from a
labour relations dispute into a potential forensic matter warranting investigation by revenue and labour
authorities.

The Documented Figures — July 2025
Gross salary on official payslip (July 2025):
R21,777.04
Salary declared to SARS / UIF by Respondents:
R27,725.66
Discrepancy:
R5,948.62
Location of R27,725.66 on payslip:
ABSENT — not in gross, net, or CTC
Month of discrepancy:
July 2025 — identical pay cycle as unlawful 40.47%
deduction

The forensic significance of this finding cannot be overstated. The leave that gave rise to the deduction —
the gap period between psychiatric admissions in June 2025 — should have been processed and deducted
in the June 2025 pay run. The Respondents instead held that recovery over to July 2025, the new financial

Page 152 of 159

012-120

012-121

153

19/5/2026-8:22:49
year, and then processed the full R14,811.77 deduction in a single pay cycle. The declared
salary figure of AM
R27,725.66 appears to reflect a pre-deduction or notional figure — a salary the Respondents reported to
government authorities as having been paid while simultaneously recovering R14,811.77 from my actual
take-home pay.
The result is a nearly R6,000 gap between what the Respondents told the government they paid me and
what I actually received. A statutory declaration to SARS or the UIF Fund that does not correspond to the
actual net remuneration paid to an employee is not an administrative oversight. It is a misrepresentation
to a government authority in a document required by law to be accurate. The fact that this
misrepresentation arises in the same month as a documented unlawful deduction — and that the leave
from which the deduction was derived arose in the previous financial year — is a structural anomaly that
a competent forensic investigator cannot ignore.
I respectfully submit that this finding elevates the matter beyond a BCEA salary deduction dispute. It
places the Respondents' payroll conduct in the category of potential statutory misrepresentation to
government authorities, and it documents a deliberate structuring of the deduction across a financial year
boundary in circumstances where the underlying leave event occurred in May2025 -start June 2025.

2. CCMA INSTITUTIONAL BIAS — FULL ACCOUNT — AND PROVINCIAL COMMISSIONER
COVER-UP
The SAHRC directed me in February 2026 to pursue CCMA remedies. I place on formal record the full
account of what occurred at conciliation, and the cover-up that followed, so that the SAHRC may assess
the quality of the remedy it directed me towards.
The conciliation hearing began with Commissioner Nthabiseng making the following statement
immediately after introductions, before I had said a single substantive word: "Nothing here relates to the
PDA." This was not a ruling made after hearing submissions. It was a declaration of a closed mind made
at the threshold of the proceedings, before I had been permitted to speak. It foreclosed the most
significant ground of my claim before the hearing began.
The Commissioner then refused to permit my opening statement. I was not allowed to place my position
on the record in an orderly fashion. The Commissioner used the proceedings to create confusion,
speaking over my submissions and introducing complications that had no basis in the documents before
her. At no point did the Commissioner engage with my BCEA violation — the statutory 25% cap under
Section 34(2) — or with the documentary evidence of the employer's own policy requiring prior HCBP
consultation. She adopted the Respondents' "no work no pay" characterisation without subjecting it to
any scrutiny. The commissioner ‘so it was for no work no pay? Okay.
When I stated my negotiation ceiling of R2.5 million for a global settlement of all claims, the
Commissioner laughed with the Respondents' representative. The Respondents then offered one month's
salary. I requested a Certificate of Non-Resolution. The proceedings were a mockery.

Page 153 of 159

012-121

012-122

154

19/5/2026-8:22:49 AM

The Johannesburg Coincidence
Commissioner Nthabiseng:
Based in Johannesburg. Presided at Cape Town conciliation.

This section documents what I can only describe as an institutional obstruction of my right of access to

My urgent high profile notice of motion application was prepared in full compliance with the Rules of the
Labour Court, ready for filing by 5 March 2026. I attempted to file online. What followed was eight days
of documented obstruction:

Labour Court Filing Obstruction — Documented Sequence
5 March 2026: Target filing date. Documents prepared in full compliance with Labour Court

deadline of end of March 2026, this sequence is not a procedural inconvenience. It is a denial of access
to the only court with jurisdiction to grant the urgent relief I need to remain housed.

3. PRELIMINARY LEGAL OBJECTION: LACK OF LOCUS STANDI &
UNCLEAN HANDS

3.1

The Applicant, AfroCentric Investment Corporation Limited, is a listed holding
company. Throughout its Supplementary Affidavit, the Applicant asserts that the
Respondent was employed exclusively by a separate, distinct subsidiary:
Medscheme Holdings (Pty) Ltd.

3.2

Paradoxically, the Applicant seeks a final interdict to suppress disclosures
regarding systemic clinical and payroll integration gaps (the Gexus/DMS
architectural flaws) on the basis that it has a "clear right" to protect proprietary
operational systems.

3.3

The Applicant cannot have it both ways. If the underlying employment
relationship, operational configurations, and statutory liabilities belong
exclusively to Medscheme Holdings (Pty) Ltd to shield the holding company from
liability, then the Applicant lacks the direct, substantial legal interest (locus
standi) to seek a final interdict in its own name.

3.4

Furthermore, the Applicant approaches this court with "unclean hands." On 19
May 2026, corporate officials acting on behalf of the group filed a Statement of
Response in the Labour Court (Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546) stating
under oath that they have "no knowledge" of these parallel proceedings. This
directly contradicts the Group CEO Gerald Neville Van Wyk's High Court
founding affidavit of 16 April 2026, which explicitly acknowledges the Labour
Court litigation. This constitutes deliberate perjury across courts to mislead
judicial officers.

PLAINTIFF'S REPLICATION TO THE DEFENDANTS' STATEMENT OF
RESPONSE

The Plaintiff, appearing in person, hereby replies as follows to the Defendants' Statement of Response
dated 19 May 2026:

1. THE THRESHOLD SPECIAL DEFENCE: PLEADING A NULLITY AND
CORPORATE IDENTITY MISREPRESENTATION
1.1 The First Defendant explicitly cited by the Plaintiff in these proceedings is AFROCENTRIC
HEALTH (PTY) LTD (Registration Number: 1996/009540/07).
1.2 The Statement of Response filed on 19 May 2026 is signed by Mr. Vijay Makenjee, who explicitly
purports to execute the signature block on page 7 "obo AFROCENTRIC RF (PTY) LTD".
1.3 AFROCENTRIC RF (PTY) LTD is a completely separate legal entity and is not a cited party to
these proceedings. A corporate official cannot legally enter a plea or defence on behalf of an un-cited
corporate entity to answer dynamic statutory and common-law claims levied against an entirely
different subsidiary.
1.4 Furthermore, the Statement of Response is fundamentally fatal as it stands completely devoid of a
Verifying Affidavit under oath. Rule 6 of the Labour Court Rules mandates that a Statement of
Response must be verified under oath by a designated corporate officer possessing direct, first-hand
personal knowledge of the operational facts.

Page 1 of 6 | Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546 | Matthee v AfroCentric Health (Pty) Ltd & Another

013-18

013-19

1.5 In its current form, the document represents nothing more than an unsworn piece of paper signed
on behalf of an outside entity. It constitutes a procedural nullity, fails to place any admissible evidence
before this Honourable Court, and must be struck out in its entirety.

2. FATAL SELECTIVE SILENCE AND IMPLIED ADMISSIONS OF
OCCUPATIONAL DETRIMENT
2.1 The Plaintiff notes that the Defendants' Statement of Response consists of blanket, superficial
denials and retreats into total, calculated silence on material factual averments that form the absolute
core of the Plaintiff's claim of an intolerable work environment and occupational detriment.
2.2 Under the rules of pleading and the established jurisprudence of South African courts, allegations
of fact that are not specifically denied, engaged with, or meaningfully answered by a respondent are
deemed to be admitted as a matter of law.
2.3 The "Wilma Incident" Silence: The Defendants completely fail to address, deny, or answer the
specific, documented operational incidents involving Wilma, which directly initiated the targeted
psychological hostility, workplace gaslighting, and systematic isolation faced by the Plaintiff.
2.4 The 30+ Day Executive Silence: The Defendants fail to provide any legal, operational, or
contractual justification for the prolonged period of more than 30 days of total administrative and
corporate silence following the Plaintiff's formal escalation of critical workplace grievances. This
complete abandonment of internal dispute resolution mechanisms objectively demonstrated to the
Plaintiff that no internal remedy was available and that the employment relationship had been broken
by management.
2.5 The CEO's Confidentiality Breach: The Defendants offer no denial, counter-narrative, or
explanation regarding the severe breach of confidentiality committed by the Group Chief Executive
Officer, who compromised the integrity of the Plaintiff's protected escalations.
2.6 By retreating into selective silence on these pivotal statutory and constitutional violations, the
Defendants have failed to establish a triable issue on whether they created an intolerable workplace.
Their calculated silence stands as an implied admission of the operational toxicity that forced the
Plaintiff's constructive dismissal.

3. DEMONSTRABLE PERJURY AND JURISDICTIONAL DECEPTION (THE CASE
NUMBER COLLISION)
3.1 In Paragraph 4 (Ad Para 6 of Part A) of their Statement of Response, signed by Vijay Makenjee
on 19 May 2026, the Defendants state under oath:
"The Defendants are not aware of any further claim in the above honorable court with
case number 2026-077546."
3.2 This statement is factually false, fraudulent, and constitutes a clear attempt to commit perjury to
mislead this Honourable Court.
3.3 On 16 April 2026, in parallel urgent proceedings before the Western Cape High Court (Case No:
2026-086906), the Group Chief Executive Officer of the Applicant's parent corporate structure,
GERALD NEVILLE VAN WYK, deposed to a Founding Affidavit under oath. In those High Court
proceedings, the Group CEO explicitly acknowledged the existence of the dynamic statutory and
financial disputes regarding the Plaintiff's remuneration and represented that the corporate structure
intended to defend both specialised actions before the Labour Court. (See Annexure WWM1)
3.4 Furthermore, the Plaintiff's specialised Application for Repayment of Unlawfully Recovered
Remuneration under Case No: 2026-077546 was formally served via electronic mail directly upon the
Group Company Secretary and Head of Legal Counsel, Lebohang Shadi Matsipa Mpumlwana, on

Page 2 of 6 | Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546 | Matthee v AfroCentric Health (Pty) Ltd & Another

013-19

013-20

13 April 2026 at 22:03. The automated electronic delivery tracking and read receipts confirm that
executive corporate legal counsel received and opened the application bundle twenty one (21) times
prior to the filing of this Response. (See Annexure WWM2)
3.5 For the Defendants to subsequently assert under oath on 19 May 2026 that they "are not aware" of
Case No: 2026-077546 is a bad-faith deception. The corporate entity is attempting to play blind in the
Labour Court to avoid default consequences, directly contradicting the sworn acknowledgments made
by its own Group CEO in the High Court. By failing to enter a legitimate appearance to defend Case
No: 2026-077546 within the mandatory 10-day statutory period, the material facts within that file stand
completely unopposed and ripe for adjudication.

4. THE UNCONTRADICTED STATUTORY CEILING VIOLATION, FACTUAL
MISREPRESENTATION, AND MALICIOUS POLICY VIOLATION (THE
RETROSPECTIVE JULY DECEPTIONS)
4.1 In Paragraph 2 (Ad Para 1 to 5 of Part A) and Paragraph 28 of their Statement of Response,
the Defendants state under oath:
"The Plaintiff was on sick leave but had exhausted annual and sick leave. The principle
of no work, no pay applied." "The Defendants maintain that the Plaintiff's July 2025
salary aligned to the days worked in July 2025..."
4.2 The Plaintiff avers that this statement is bad in law and constitutes a flagrant factual
misrepresentation explicitly designed to mislead this Honourable Court.
4.3 The Defendants assert that the July 2025 salary reduction was an automatic operational "alignment
to days worked in July 2025." This is mathematically and operationally impossible. The Plaintiff's
minor, documented absences in July 2025 consisted strictly of 1 to 3 isolated days utilised to attend
medical appointments following his discharge from hospital.
4.4 Had the Defendants genuinely applied a live, real-time "no work, no pay" alignment strictly for the
days missed in July 2025, the total operational deduction would have been limited to a minor fraction
of his earnings (representing approximately 1 to 3 daily operational units).
4.5 Instead, the Defendants processed a massive, destructive extraction totalling R14,811.77. The sheer
volume of this extraction demonstrates that the July 2025 payslip was weaponised to execute a
retrospective clawback for historical, disputed days stretching back into the preceding months of May
and June 2025.
4.6 The true operational context of this extraction demonstrates malice. Immediately upon the Plaintiff's
physical discharge and return to work from a registered Mental Health Institution (where he was treated
for severe PTSD and depression), the Second Defendant's management aggressively bypassed a
humane, structured back-to-work reintegration. Instead of allowing the Plaintiff a reasonable window
to resettle into his occupational functions, management immediately forced an adversarial meeting to
confront him.
4.7 During this meeting, the Plaintiff was brutally honest regarding his acute psychiatric vulnerability,
his financial constraints, and his desperate need for structural stability. In response to this medical
disclosure, the Second Defendant's manager issued a hostile follow-up electronic mail message actively
misrepresenting corporate protocols, stating: "We don't allow staggering. We are not a loan company."
(See Annexure H in Statement of claim)
4.8 The statement that the corporate structure "does not allow staggering" is a demonstrable, written
deception. The Defendants' own operative Human Capital Business Partner (HCBP) Policy explicitly
mandates that any payroll corrections or historical leave recoveries must be handled via a structured
consultation process, with an express provision allowing for staggered recoveries over multiple pay
cycles to preserve an employee's basic livelihood. (See Annexure J in Statement of claim)

Page 3 of 6 | Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546 | Matthee v AfroCentric Health (Pty) Ltd & Another

013-20

013-21

4.9 By attempting to disguise a massive, retrospective historical clawback as a real-time current-month
alignment, and by deploying a hostile administrative narrative (In Paragraph 16[“and do not grant
loans.”, “WE DO NOT ALLOW STAGGERING”]) to deny a vulnerable employee the protection of
their own internal policy, the Defendants have exposed the targeted, retaliatory nature of their payroll
administration.
4.10 Even if the Defendants mistakenly believed they possessed a unilateral right to recover historical
days from May and June, they were strictly bound by Section 34 of the Basic Conditions of Employment
Act 75 of 1997 ("BCEA"). Section 34(1) strictly prohibits any reduction from an employee's
remuneration without express written consent. The Plaintiff at no stage provided written consent for
this financial extraction.
4.11 Crucially, Section 34(2) of the BCEA establishes an absolute statutory ceiling, explicitly dictating
that even where a retrospective recovery is legally permissible to correct an operational leave balance
or overpayment, the total aggregate amount of the reduction may not exceed one-quarter (25%) of
the employee's gross monthly monetary remuneration.
4.12 The Plaintiff's verified July 2025 payslip (see Annexure I of statement of claim) reflects an
unlawful configuration completely outside the boundary of the law:
• Contractual Gross Normal Earnings: R36,588.81
• Retrospective Recovery Reductions: R14,811.77
• Effective Remuneration Reduction Percentage: 40.47%
4.13 By formally admitting they executed a recovery that stripped away 40.47% of an employee's
monthly livelihood in a single pay cycle — under the false pretence of a live monthly alignment, while
actively lying about internal policy provisions — the Defendants have placed an ex facie illegal act
before this Court.
4.14 This Honourable Court possesses no equitable or judicial discretion to condone an express
violation of Section 34(2), nor can it validate a defence built on an objective factual falsehood. The
statutory 25% boundary is absolute and immutable. A deduction of 40.47% is illegal on its face,
rendering the recovery an unlawful expropriation of remuneration as an absolute matter of law. Liability
is fully established on the face of the papers.

5. THE REJECTION OF THE WEAPONISED "INSUBORDINATION"
REPRIMAND
5.1 In Paragraph 26, the Defendants introduce a disciplinary narrative, asserting that the Plaintiff was
"reprimanded for insubordination" because he refused an instruction to directly engage with a client
after an internal investigation.
5.2 The Plaintiff fiercely denies that this reprimand constituted a lawful or reasonable operational
action. The record demonstrates that this disciplinary charge was retroactively weaponised against the
Plaintiff only after he escalated Protected Disclosures regarding systemic clinical integration defects
within the Gexus-DMS architecture. (See Annexure N date of statement of claim 23rd October 2025 See
Annexure O date of statement of claim 31 October 2025 “ Insubordination reprimand on the 31st
October 2025 for 23rd October 2025 protected disclosure.”)
5.3 The instruction given to the Plaintiff was an unlawful and unethical command to interface with a
client for the purpose of managing, obscuring, or smoothing over un-remedied system errors that
resulted in erroneous non-adherence letters being sent to vulnerable medical scheme beneficiaries.
5.4 In South African employment law, an employee is only bound to obey instructions that are lawful,
reasonable, and ethical. Refusing to participate in corporate obfuscation or to validate an unresolved
operational gap does not constitute actionable insubordination. The reprimand was a textbook act of
occupational detriment and workplace retaliation in direct violation of the Protected Disclosures Act 26
of 2000 ("PDA").
Page 4 of 6 | Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546 | Matthee v AfroCentric Health (Pty) Ltd & Another

013-21

013-22

6. THE UNTENABILITY OF THE CONSTRUCTIVE DISMISSAL DENIAL
6.1 In Paragraphs 29 and 33, the Defendants deny creating an intolerable work environment and
assert that the Plaintiff resigned prematurely while internal grievance timelines were still unfolding.
6.2 The Plaintiff rejects this assertion. Under prevailing labour jurisprudence, a self-represented
employee is not required to endure structural destitution, bad-faith delays, and medical hostility
indefinitely while an employer deploys strategic, administrative inertia.
6.3 The intolerability of the environment must be assessed objectively. The Defendants actively
subjected the Plaintiff to a severe 40.47% financial reduction, stripped away his means of physical
survival, ignored critical medical correspondence regarding his diagnosed PTSD and severe depression,
and permitted their Employee Relations department to file sworn text labelling his psychiatric condition
a subjective interpretation.
6.4 Expecting an employee with a formally disclosed mental health disability to remain embedded in
an environment characterised by severe financial deprivation and weaponised psychological attacks is
objectively unconscionable. The Defendants' systemic conduct and profound structural neglect rendered
the continuation of the employment relationship entirely intolerable, satisfying the full statutory criteria
for a constructive dismissal under Section 186(1)(e) of the Labour Relations Act 66 of 1995.

7. CONCLUSION AND PRAYER FOR RELIEF
7.1 The Defendants' Statement of Response is procedurally dead on arrival for lack of a verifying
affidavit and for being signed on behalf of an un-cited, non-party entity. Substantively, it collapses into
a direct liquidated admission of an illegal 40.47% remuneration reduction under the BCEA, built upon
an objective factual misrepresentation regarding the Plaintiff's July 2025 attendance.
7.2 There is no valid, sworn triable defence placed before this Honourable Court by the Respondents
to counter the clear, documented, and statutory violations presented by the Applicant.
WHEREFORE the Plaintiff persists in the claims set out in his Statement of Claim and prays for an
order:
IN RESPECT OF THE THRESHOLD PROCEDURAL APPLICATION:
1.

Striking out the Defendants’ Statement of Response dated 19 May 2026 as a procedural
nullity, on the grounds that it is unverified by affidavit and purports to have been filed on behalf
of a non-cited juristic entity, namely AfroCentric RF (Pty) Ltd.

IN RESPECT OF THE CONCURRENT APPLICATION (CASE NO: 2026-077546):

3. An order compelling the First and Second Defendants, jointly and severally, the one paying the

misconduct.

RESPONDENT'S ANSWERING AFFIDAVIT TO THE APPLICANT'S
SUPPLEMENTARY FOUNDING AFFIDAVIT

I, the undersigned,
WILBUR WILLIAM MATTHEE
do hereby make oath and state:

1. THE DEPONENT AND STATUS
1.1

I am the Respondent in this matter. I am an adult male, a Specialist Registered
Nurse, a Health Services Manager holding a Postgraduate Diploma in Health
Services Management (NQF Level 8) awarded with distinction, and the founder
of Ethic Hawks.

1.2

I act in person. The facts contained in this affidavit fall within my personal
knowledge, save where the context indicates otherwise, and are both true and
correct.
2. PURPOSE OF THIS AFFIDAVIT

2.1

This affidavit is filed to answer the Applicant's Supplementary Founding
Affidavit deposed to by Lebohang Shadi Matsipa Mpumlwana on 4 May 2026.

013-61

013-62

2.2

The primary objective of this affidavit is to expose a fatal corporate "shell game"
executed by the Applicant. The Applicant seeks the equitable relief of a final
interdict in this Honourable Court while systematically using its subsidiaries to
commit perjury, withhold statutory exit documentation, and manipulate
jurisdictions across the High Court and the Labour Court.

2.3

This affidavit incorporates a comprehensive Bare Denials Analysis and an
itemised Schedule of Perjuries and Corporate Misrepresentations that strip the
Applicant of standing (locus standi) and the requisite "Clean Hands" required for
a final interdict.
3. PRELIMINARY LEGAL OBJECTION: LACK OF LOCUS STANDI &
UNCLEAN HANDS

3.1

The Applicant, AfroCentric Investment Corporation Limited, is a listed holding
company. Throughout its Supplementary Affidavit, the Applicant asserts that the
Respondent was employed exclusively by a separate, distinct subsidiary:
Medscheme Holdings (Pty) Ltd.

3.2

Paradoxically, the Applicant seeks a final interdict to suppress disclosures
regarding systemic clinical and payroll integration gaps (the Gexus/DMS
architectural flaws) on the basis that it has a "clear right" to protect proprietary
operational systems.

3.3

The Applicant cannot have it both ways. If the underlying employment

corporate entity to answer dynamic statutory and common-law claims levied against an entirely
different subsidiary.
1.4 Furthermore, the Statement of Response is fundamentally fatal as it stands completely devoid of a
Verifying Affidavit under oath. Rule 6 of the Labour Court Rules mandates that a Statement of
Response must be verified under oath by a designated corporate officer possessing direct, first-hand
personal knowledge of the operational facts.

4. THE UNCONTRADICTED STATUTORY CEILING VIOLATION, FACTUAL
MISREPRESENTATION, AND MALICIOUS POLICY VIOLATION (THE
RETROSPECTIVE JULY DECEPTIONS)
4.1 In Paragraph 2 (Ad Para 1 to 5 of Part A) and Paragraph 28 of their Statement of Response,
the Defendants state under oath:
"The Plaintiff was on sick leave but had exhausted annual and sick leave. The principle
of no work, no pay applied." "The Defendants maintain that the Plaintiff's July 2025
salary aligned to the days worked in July 2025..."
4.2 The Plaintiff avers that this statement is bad in law and constitutes a flagrant factual
misrepresentation explicitly designed to mislead this Honourable Court.
4.3 The Defendants assert that the July 2025 salary reduction was an automatic operational "alignment
to days worked in July 2025." This is mathematically and operationally impossible. The Plaintiff's
minor, documented absences in July 2025 consisted strictly of 1 to 3 isolated days utilised to attend
medical appointments following his discharge from hospital.
4.4 Had the Defendants genuinely applied a live, real-time "no work, no pay" alignment strictly for the
days missed in July 2025, the total operational deduction would have been limited to a minor fraction
of his earnings (representing approximately 1 to 3 daily operational units).
4.5 Instead, the Defendants processed a massive, destructive extraction totalling R14,811.77. The sheer
volume of this extraction demonstrates that the July 2025 payslip was weaponised to execute a
retrospective clawback for historical, disputed days stretching back into the preceding months of May
and June 2025.
4.6 The true operational context of this extraction demonstrates malice. Immediately upon the Plaintiff's
physical discharge and return to work from a registered Mental Health Institution (where he was treated
for severe PTSD and depression), the Second Defendant's management aggressively bypassed a
humane, structured back-to-work reintegration. Instead of allowing the Plaintiff a reasonable window
to resettle into his occupational functions, management immediately forced an adversarial meeting to
confront him.
4.7 During this meeting, the Plaintiff was brutally honest regarding his acute psychiatric vulnerability,
his financial constraints, and his desperate need for structural stability. In response to this medical
disclosure, the Second Defendant's manager issued a hostile follow-up electronic mail message actively
misrepresenting corporate protocols, stating: "We don't allow staggering. We are not a loan company."
(See Annexure H in Statement of claim)
4.8 The statement that the corporate structure "does not allow staggering" is a demonstrable, written
deception. The Defendants' own operative Human Capital Business Partner (HCBP) Policy explicitly
mandates that any payroll corrections or historical leave recoveries must be handled via a structured
consultation process, with an express provision allowing for staggered recoveries over multiple pay
cycles to preserve an employee's basic livelihood. (See Annexure J in Statement of claim)

Page 3 of 6 | Case No: 2026-083299 / 2026-077546 | Matthee v AfroCentric Health (Pty) Ltd & Another

013-80

013-81

4.9 By attempting to disguise a massive, retrospective historical clawback as a real-time current-month
alignment, and by deploying a hostile administrative narrative (In Paragraph 16[“and do not grant
loans.”, “WE DO NOT ALLOW STAGGERING”]) to deny a vulnerable employee the protection of
their own internal policy, the Defendants have exposed the targeted, retaliatory nature of their payroll
administration.
4.10 Even if the Defendants mistakenly believed they possessed a unilateral right to recover historical
days from May and June, they were strictly bound by Section 34 of the Basic Conditions of Employment
Act 75 of 1997 ("BCEA"). Section 34(1) strictly prohibits any reduction from an employee's
remuneration without express written consent. The Plaintiff at no stage provided written consent for
this financial extraction.
4.11 Crucially, Section 34(2) of the BCEA establishes an absolute statutory ceiling, explicitly dictating
that even where a retrospective recovery is legally permissible to correct an operational leave balance
or overpayment, the total aggregate amount of the reduction may not exceed one-quarter (25%) of
the employee's gross monthly monetary remuneration.
4.12 The Plaintiff's verified July 2025 payslip (see Annexure I of statement of claim) reflects an
unlawful configuration completely outside the boundary of the law:
• Contractual Gross Normal Earnings: R36,588.81
• Retrospective Recovery Reductions: R14,811.77
• Effective Remuneration Reduction Percentage: 40.47%
4.13 By formally admitting they executed a recovery that stripped away 40.47% of an employee's
monthly livelihood in a single pay cycle — under the false pretence of a live monthly alignment, while
actively lying about internal policy provisions — the Defendants have placed an ex facie illegal act
before this Court.
4.14 This Honourable Court possesses no equitable or judicial discretion to condone an express
violation of Section 34(2), nor can it validate a defence built on an objective factual falsehood. The
statutory 25% boundary is absolute and immutable. A deduction of 40.47% is illegal on its face,
rendering the recovery an unlawful expropriation of remuneration as an absolute matter of law. Liability
is fully established on the face of the papers.

5. THE REJECTION OF THE WEAPONISED "INSUBORDINATION"
REPRIMAND
5.1 In Paragraph 26, the Defendants introduce a disciplinary narrative, asserting that the Plaintiff was
"reprimanded for insubordination" because he refused an instruction to directly engage with a client
after an internal investigation.
5.2 The Plaintiff fiercely denies that this reprimand constituted a lawful or reasonable operational
action. The record demonstrates that this disciplinary charge was retroactively weaponised against the
Plaintiff only after he escalated Protected Disclosures regarding systemic clinical integration defects
within the Gexus-DMS architecture. (See Annexure N date of statement of claim 23rd October 2025 See
Annexure O date of statement of claim 31 October 2025 “ Insubordination reprimand on the 31st
October 2025 for 23rd October 2025 protected disclosure.”)
5.3 The instruction given to the Plaintiff was an unlawful and unethical command to interface with a
client for the purpose of managing, obscuring, or smoothing over un-remedied system errors that
resulted in erroneous non-adherence letters being sent to vulnerable medical scheme beneficiaries.
5.4 In South African employment law, an employee is only bound to obey instructions that are lawful,
reasonable, and ethical. Refusing to participate in corporate obfuscation or to validate an unresolved
operational gap does not constitute actionable insubordination. The reprimand was a textbook act of
occupational detriment and workplace retaliation in direct violation of the Protected Disclosures Act 26
of 2000 ("PDA").
